capita</div></th><td>\n$31,797</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="line-height:11pt"><b>Website</b><br /><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.osce.org/">www.osce.org</a></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</b> (<b>OSCE</b>) is the world\'s largest security-oriented <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organization</a>. Its mandate includes issues such as <a href="/wiki/Arms_control" title="Arms control">arms control</a>, promotion of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a>, and fair elections. It employs around 3,460 people, mostly in its field operations but also in its secretariat in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and its institutions. It has its origins in the 1975 Conference on Security and Co-operation in Europe (CSCE) held in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, Finland.\n</p><p>The OSCE is concerned with early warning, conflict prevention, <a href="/wiki/Crisis_management" title="Crisis management">crisis management</a>, and post-conflict rehabilitation. Its 57 participating states are located in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, northern and central <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_America" title="Northern America">North America</a>. The participating states cover much of the land area of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a>. It was created during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> era as an East\xe2\x80\x93West forum.<sup id="cite_ref-galbreath_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-galbreath-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 href="#Relations_with_the_United_Nations"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Relations with the United Nations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#The_three_dimensions"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">The three dimensions</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a tocsection-16"><a href="#Economic_and_environmental_dimension_(second_dimension)"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Economic and environmental dimension (second dimension)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Human_dimension_(third_dimension)"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Human dimension (third dimension)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#OSCE_Democracy_Defender_Award"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">OSCE Democracy Defender Award</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Criticism"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#OSCE_Parliamentary_Assembly"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">OSCE Parliamentary Assembly</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#2012_Texas_controversy"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">2012 Texas controversy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#War_in_Donbass"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">War in Donbass</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Turkey"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">Turkey</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314,_Helsinki,_KSZE-Konferenz,_Schlussakte.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314%2C_Helsinki%2C_KSZE-Konferenz%2C_Schlussakte.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314%2C_Helsinki%2C_KSZE-Konferenz%2C_Schlussakte.jpg" width="250" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314%2C_Helsinki%2C_KSZE-Konferenz%2C_Schlussakte.jpg/375px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314%2C_Helsinki%2C_KSZE-Konferenz%2C_Schlussakte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314%2C_Helsinki%2C_KSZE-Konferenz%2C_Schlussakte.jpg/500px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314%2C_Helsinki%2C_KSZE-Konferenz%2C_Schlussakte.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="542" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-P0805-314,_Helsinki,_KSZE-Konferenz,_Schlussakte.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Helmut_Schmidt" title="Helmut Schmidt">Helmut Schmidt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erich_Honecker" title="Erich Honecker">Erich Honecker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Kreisky" title="Bruno Kreisky">Bruno Kreisky</a> at the 1975 CSCE summit in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, Finland.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Organization has its roots in the 1973 <b>Conference on Security and Co-operation in Europe</b> (CSCE). Talks had been mooted about a European security grouping since the 1950s but the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> prevented any substantial progress until the talks at <a href="/wiki/Dipoli" title="Dipoli">Dipoli</a> in <a href="/wiki/Espoo" title="Espoo">Espoo</a> began in November 1972. These talks were held at the suggestion of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> which wished to use the talks to maintain its control over the <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> countries in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Finland" title="President of Finland">President of Finland</a> <a href="/wiki/Urho_Kekkonen" title="Urho Kekkonen">Urho Kekkonen</a> hosted them in order to bolster his <a href="/wiki/Paasikivi-Kekkonen_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Paasikivi-Kekkonen line">policy of neutrality</a>. <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, however, saw these talks as a way to reduce the tension in the region, furthering economic cooperation and obtaining humanitarian improvements for the populations of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Communist bloc</a>.\n</p><p>The recommendations of the talks, in the form of "The Blue Book", gave the practical foundations for a three-stage conference called the "Helsinki process".<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The CSCE opened in Helsinki on 3 July 1973 with 35 states sending representatives. Stage&#160;I only took five days to agree to follow the Blue Book. Stage&#160;II was the main working phase and was conducted in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> from 18 September 1973 until 21 July 1975. The result of Stage&#160;II was the <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Accords" title="Helsinki Accords">Helsinki Final Act</a> which was signed by the 35 participating states during Stage&#160;III, which took place in <a href="/wiki/Finlandia_Hall" title="Finlandia Hall">Finlandia Hall</a> from 30 July \xe2\x80\x93 1 August 1975. It was opened by <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>\xe2\x80\x99s diplomat Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Agostino_Casaroli" title="Agostino Casaroli">Agostino Casaroli</a>, who was chairman of the conference.\n</p><p>The concepts of improving relations and implementing the act were developed over a series of follow-up meetings, with major gatherings in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> (4 October 1977&#160;&#8211;&#32;8 March 1978), <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> (11 November 1980&#160;&#8211;&#32;9 September 1983) and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> (4 November 1986&#160;&#8211;&#32;19 January 1989).\n</p><p>The collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> required a change of role for the CSCE. The <a href="/wiki/Paris_Charter" title="Paris Charter">Charter of Paris for a New Europe</a>, signed on 21 November 1990, marked the beginning of this change. With the changes capped by the renaming of the CSCE to the OSCE on 1 January 1995, in accord with the results of the conference held in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, Hungary, in 1994. The OSCE now had a formal secretariat, Senior Council, Parliamentary Assembly, Conflict Prevention Centre, and Office for Free Elections (later becoming the Office for Democratic Institutions and Human Rights).\n</p><p>In December 1996, the "<a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> Declaration on a Common and Comprehensive Security Model for Europe for the Twenty-First Century" affirmed the universal and indivisible nature of security on the European continent.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> on 19 November 1999, the OSCE ended a two-day summit by calling for a political settlement in <a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechnya</a> and adopting a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Charter_for_European_Security&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Charter for European Security (page does not exist)">Charter for European Security</a>. According to then Minister of Foreign Affairs <a href="/wiki/Igor_Ivanov" title="Igor Ivanov">Igor Ivanov</a>, this summit marked a turning point in Russian perception of the OSCE, from an organization that expressed Europe\'s collective will, to an organization that serves as a <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> tool for "forced democratization".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Through its Office for Democratic Institutions and Human Rights (ODIHR), the OSCE observes and assesses elections in its member states, in order to support fair and transparent democratic processes, in keeping with the mutual standards to which the organization is committed;<sup id="cite_ref-cns2004_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cns2004-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> between 1994 and 2004 the OSCE sent teams of observers to monitor more than 150 elections, typically focusing on elections in emerging democracies.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday2004_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday2004-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, at the invitation of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> Government, the ODIHR deployed an assessment mission, made up of participants from six OSCE member states, which observed that year\'s US presidential election and produced a report.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It was the first time that a US presidential election was the subject of OSCE monitoring, although the organization had previously monitored state-level American elections in Florida and California, in 2002 and 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday2004_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday2004-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The 2004 assessment took place against the backdrop of the controversial recount effort in the 2000 US presidential election,<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday2004_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday2004-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and came about largely through the initiative of 13 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> members of the  <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>. That group, which included <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Lee" title="Barbara Lee">Barbara Lee</a>, of California, and <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Bernice_Johnson" title="Eddie Bernice Johnson">Eddie Bernice Johnson</a>, of Texas, initially addressed a request for election observers to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, in a letter to <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a>, but the request was declined.<sup id="cite_ref-cns2004_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cns2004-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, the administration of <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, through the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">State Department</a>, headed by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">Colin Powell</a>, responded to the lawmakers\' concerns by inviting the OSCE election-monitoring mission.<sup id="cite_ref-cns2004_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cns2004-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The five official languages of the OSCE are <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_states">Participating states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: title="Australia">Australia</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></td>\n</tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">Legal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Legal status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A unique aspect of the OSCE is the non-binding status of its constitutive charter. Rather than being a formal <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">treaty</a> ratified by national <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislatures</a>, the Helsinki Final Act represents a political commitment by the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">heads of government</a> of all signatories to build security and cooperation in Europe on the basis of its provisions. This allows the OSCE to remain a flexible <i>process</i> for the evolution of improved cooperation, which avoids disputes and/or sanctions over implementation. By agreeing to these commitments, signatories for the first time accepted that treatment of citizens <i>within</i> their borders was also a matter of legitimate international concern.  This open process of the OSCE is often given credit for helping build democracy in the Soviet Union and Eastern Europe, thus leading to the end of the Cold War<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Unlike most international intergovernmental organizations, however, the OSCE does not have international legal personality on account of the lack of legal effect of its charter.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> As a result, its headquarters\xe2\x80\x99 host, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, had to confer legal personality on the organization in order to be able to sign a legal agreement regarding its presence in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure_and_institutions">Structure and institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Structure and institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Political direction to the organization is given by heads of state or government during summits. Summits are not regular or scheduled but held as needed. The last summit took place in Astana (Kazakhstan), on 1 and 2 December 2010. The high-level decision-making body of the organization is the Ministerial Council, which meets at the end of every year. At ambassadorial level the Permanent Council convenes weekly in Vienna and serves as the regular negotiating and decision-making body. The chairperson of the Permanent Council is the ambassador to the Organization of the participating State which holds the chairmanship. From 1 January 2017 to 31 December 2017 the Chairperson-in-Office is Austrian Foreign Minister, Sebastian Kurz, who succeeded German Foreign Minister Frank-Walter Steinmeier.\n</p><p>In addition to the Ministerial Council and Permanent Council, the Forum for Security Co-operation is also an OSCE decision-making body. It deals predominantly with matters of military co-operation, such as modalities for inspections according to the Vienna Document of 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The OSCE\'s Secretariat is located in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>. The current Secretary General is <a href="/wiki/Lamberto_Zannier" title="Lamberto Zannier">Lamberto Zannier</a> of Italy, who took over from <a href="/wiki/Marc_Perrin_de_Brichambaut" title="Marc Perrin de Brichambaut">Marc Perrin de Brichambaut</a> of France.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The organization also has offices in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw,_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw, Poland">Warsaw</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG/220px-OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG" width="220" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG/330px-OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG/440px-OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2412" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OSCE-Permanent_Council.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A meeting of the OSCE Permanent Council at the <a href="/wiki/Hofburg" title="Hofburg">Hofburg</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>As of  March&#160;2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the OSCE employed 3,462 staff, including 513 in its secretariat and institutions and 2,949 in its 17 field operations.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> is made up of 323 parliamentarians from 57 member states. The Parliamentary Assembly performs its functions mainly via the Standing Committee, the Bureau, and 3 General Committees (Committee on Political Affairs and Security, Committee on Economic Affairs, Science, Technology and Environment, and Committee on Democracy, Human Rights and Humanitarian Questions).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The Parliamentary Assembly passes resolutions on matters such as political and security affairs, economic and environmental issues, and democracy and human rights. Representing the collective voice of OSCE parliamentarians, these resolutions and recommendations are meant to ensure that all participating states live up to their OSCE commitments. The Parliamentary Assembly also engages in parliamentary diplomacy, and has an extensive election observation program.\n</p><p>The oldest OSCE institution is the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_Democratic_Institutions_and_Human_Rights" title="Office for Democratic Institutions and Human Rights">Office for Democratic Institutions and Human Rights</a> (ODIHR), established in 1991 following a decision made at the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Charter" title="Paris Charter">Summit of Paris</a>. It is based in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, and is active throughout the OSCE area in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Election_observer" class="mw-redirect" title="Election observer">election observation</a>, democratic development, human rights, tolerance and non-discrimination, rule of law, and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a> issues. The ODIHR has observed over 300 elections and referendums since 1995, sending more than 50,000 observers. It has operated outside its own area twice, sending a team that offered technical support to the 9 October 2004 presidential elections in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, an OSCE Partner for Co-operation, and an election support team to assist with parliamentary and provincial council elections on 18 September 2005. ODIHR is headed by Michael Georg Link.\n</p><p>The Office of the <a href="/wiki/OSCE_Representative_on_Freedom_of_the_Media" title="OSCE Representative on Freedom of the Media">OSCE Representative on Freedom of the Media</a>, established in December 1997, acts as a watchdog to provide early warning on violations of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of expression">freedom of expression</a> in OSCE participating States. The representative also assists participating States by advocating and promoting full compliance with OSCE norms, principles and commitments regarding freedom of expression and free media. As of 2011, the current representative is expert in media law from Bosnia and Herzegovina <a href="/wiki/Dunja_Mijatovic" class="mw-redirect" title="Dunja Mijatovic">Dunja Mijatovic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_on_National_Minorities" title="High Commissioner on National Minorities">High Commissioner on National Minorities</a> was created on 8 July 1992 by the Helsinki Summit Meeting of the Conference on Security and Cooperation in Europe. It is charged with identifying and seeking early resolution of ethnic tension that might endanger peace, stability or friendly relations between participating states.\n</p><p>Each year the OSCE holds an OSCE Asian Conference with partner nations like Australia, Thailand, South Korea, Kazakhstan and Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-osceasianconf_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osceasianconf-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Secretary_General">Secretary General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Secretary General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The incumbent of this post acts as the representative of the Chairperson-in-Office, and as the OSCE\'s chief administrative officer. href="/wiki/Thomas_Greminger" title="Thomas Greminger">Thomas Greminger</a> (2017\xe2\x80\x93)</li></ol>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chairmanship">Chairmanship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chairmanship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hofburg_OSCE.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Hofburg_OSCE.JPG/220px-Hofburg_OSCE.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Hofburg_OSCE.JPG/330px-Hofburg_OSCE.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Hofburg_OSCE.JPG/440px-Hofburg_OSCE.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hofburg_OSCE.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>OSCE Permanent Council venue at the <a href="/wiki/Hofburg" title="Hofburg">Hofburg</a>, Vienna.</div></div></div>\n<p>The responsibilities of the Chairman-in-Office (CiO) include\n</p>\n<ul><li>co-ordination of the work of OSCE institutions;</li>\n<li>representing the Organization;</li>\n<li>supervising activities related to conflict prevention, crisis management and post-conflict rehabilitation.</li></ul>\n<p>The chairmanship rotates annually, and the post of the chairman-in-office is held by the foreign minister of the participating State which holds the chairmanship. The CiO is assisted by the previous and incoming chairman-in-office; the three of them together constitute the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/troika" class="extiw" title="wikt:troika">Troika</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The origin of the institution lies with the Charter of Paris for a New Europe (1990), the Helsinki Document 1992 formally institutionalized this function.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summits_of_heads_of_State_and_Government">Summits of heads of State and Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Summits of heads of State and Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:95%;line-height:1.3em;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Summit</th>\n<th>Date</th>\n<th>Location</th>\n<th>Country</th>\n<th>Decisions\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>I</td>\n<td style="white-space:nowrap;">30 July \xe2\x80\x93 1 August 1975</td>\n<td>Helsinki</td>\n<td style="white-space:nowrap;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1100" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>\n</td>\n<td>Closing of the Conference on Security and Cooperation in Europe (CSCE). The table below shows the holders since 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:95%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Country</th>\n<th>Chairman-in-Office\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1991</td>\n<td style="white-space:nowrap;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, Laj\xc4\x8d\xc3\xa1k</a></i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiscal_history">Fiscal history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fiscal history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since 1993, the OSCE\'s budget by year (in millions of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a>,) has been:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r853265166"/><table class="multicol" style=";border-spacing:0;background:transparent;" role="presentation">\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n<td style="width:15.0em;;;">\n<ul><li>2018 ... \xe2\x82\xac137.8 million <sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2017 ... \xe2\x82\xac139.0 million</li>\n<li>2016 ... \xe2\x82\xac141.1 million</li>\n<li>2015 ... \xe2\x82\xac141.1 million</li>\n<li>2014 ... ... \xe2\x82\xac21 million</li>\n<li>1993 ... \xe2\x82\xac12 million</li></ul></td>\n</tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_9453e9ca14960bc47a9c6fdc0c8f4a2d"></map><img usemap="#timeline_9453e9ca14960bc47a9c6fdc0c8f4a2d" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/9453e9ca14960bc47a9c6fdc0c8f4a2d.png" /></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_the_United_Nations">Relations with the United Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Relations with the United Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The OSCE considers itself a regional organization in the sense of <a href="/wiki/Chapter_VIII_of_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Chapter VIII of the United Nations Charter">Chapter VIII of the United Nations Charter</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and is an <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">observer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_ARES485_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_ARES485-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>  The Chairman-in-Office gives routine briefings to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_three_dimensions">The three dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The three dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Politico-military_dimension_.28first_dimension.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Politico-military_dimension_(first_dimension)">Politico-military dimension (first dimension)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politico-military dimension (first dimension)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The OSCE takes a comprehensive approach to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Politico-military&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Politico-military (page does not exist)">politico-military</a> dimension of security, which includes a number of commitments by participating States and mechanisms for conflict prevention and resolution. The organization also seeks to enhance military security by promoting greater openness, transparency and co-operation.\n</p>\n<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Arms_control" title="Arms control">Arms control</a><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<p>The end of the Cold War resulted in a huge amount of surplus weapons becoming available in what is known as the international <a href="/wiki/Grey_market" title="Grey market">grey market</a> for weapons. The OSCE helps to stop the - often illegal - spread of such weapons and offers assistance with their destruction.  The OSCE hosts the annual exchange of information under the <a href="/wiki/Conventional_Forces_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Conventional Forces in Europe">Conventional Forces in Europe</a> treaty.  The OSCE has also implemented two additional exchanges of information, the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Document" title="Vienna Document">Vienna Document</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_Exchange_of_Military_Information" title="Global Exchange of Military Information">Global Exchange of Military Information</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/Open_Skies_Consultative_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Skies Consultative Commission">Open Skies Consultative Commission</a>, the implementing body for the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Open_Skies" title="Treaty on Open Skies">Treaty on Open Skies</a>, meets monthly at its Vienna headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Border management<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<p>The actions taken by the OSCE in border monitoring range from conflict prevention to post-conflict management, capacity building and institutional support.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Combating terrorism<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<p>With its expertise in conflict prevention, crisis management and early warning, the OSCE contributes to worldwide efforts in <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">combating terrorism</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Conflict prevention<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<p>The OSCE works to prevent conflicts from arising and to facilitate lasting comprehensive political settlements for existing conflicts. It also helps with the process of rehabilitation in post-conflict areas.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Military reform</dt></dl>\n<p>The OSCE\'s Forum for Security Co-operation provides a framework for political dialogue on military reform, while practical activities are conducted by field operations, as well as the Conflict Prevention Centre.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Policing</dt></dl>\n<p>OSCE police operations are an integral part of the organization\'s efforts in conflict prevention and post-conflict rehabilitation.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Implementation</dt></dl>\n<p>The OSCE was a rather small organization until selection by the international community to provide electoral organization to post war Bosnia and Herzegovina in early 1996. Ambassador Frowick was the first OSCE representative to initiate national election in September 1996, human rights issues and rule of law specifically designed to provide a foundation for judicial organization within Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n</p><p>The OSCE had regional offices and field offices, to include the office in Brcko in northeastern Bosnia and Herzegovina which remained in limbo until the Brcko Arbitration Agreement could be decided, finalized and implemented.\n</p><p>Brcko become a "special district" and remains so today.\n</p><p>The OSCE essentially took the place of the United Nations in Bosnia and Herzegovina in part because the Bosnian leadership felt deep contempt for the UN efforts to stop the war which began in 1991 and ended in 1995. During the time the United Nations were attempting a political solution, thousands of UN troops were posted in and around Bosnia and Herzegovina with special emphasis on Sarajevo. Between the inclusive dates of 1991 through 1995, over 200,000 Bosnians were killed and over one million displaced and another million as refugees. <a href="/wiki/Citation_needed" title="Citation needed">citation needed</a>\n</p><p>The OSCE continues to have a presence and a number of initiatives to bring a sustained peace to the region.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Economic_and_environmental_dimension_.28second_dimension.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_and_environmental_dimension_(second_dimension)">Economic and environmental dimension (second dimension)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economic and environmental dimension (second dimension)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(February 2012)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Activities in the economic and environmental dimension include the monitoring of developments related to economic and environmental security in OSCE participating States, with the aim of alerting them to any threat of conflict; assisting States in the creation of economic and environmental policies, legislation and institutions to promote security in the OSCE region.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Economic activities</dt></dl>\n<p>Among the economic activities of the OSCE feature activities related to migration management, transport and energy security. Most activities are implemented in co-operation with partner organizations.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Environmental activities</dt></dl>\n<p>The OSCE has developed a range of activities in the environmental sphere aimed at addressing ecologic threats to security in its participating States. Among the activities feature projects in the area of hazardous waste, water management and access to information under the <a href="/wiki/Aarhus_Convention" title="Aarhus Convention">Aarhus Convention</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Human_dimension_.28third_dimension.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_dimension_(third_dimension)">Human dimension (third dimension)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Human dimension (third dimension)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The commitments made by OSCE participating States in the <a href="/wiki/Three_generations_of_human_rights" title="Three generations of human rights">human dimension</a> aim to ensure full respect for human rights and fundamental freedoms; to abide by the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>; to promote the principles of democracy by building, strengthening and protecting democratic institutions; and to promote <a href="/wiki/Toleration" title="Toleration">tolerance</a> throughout the OSCE region.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Combating trafficking in human beings</dt></dl>\n<p>Since 2003 the OSCE<sup id="cite_ref-osce.org_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osce.org-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> has had an established mechanism for combating trafficking in human beings, as defined by Article 3 of the <a href="/wiki/Convention_against_Transnational_Organized_Crime" class="mw-redirect" title="Convention against Transnational Organized Crime">Palermo Protocol</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> which is aimed at raising public awareness of the problem and building the political will within participating states to tackle it effectively.\n</p><p>The OSCE actions against <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">trafficking in human beings</a> are coordinated by the Office of the Special Representative and Co-ordinator for Combating Trafficking in Human Beings.<sup id="cite_ref-osce.org_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osce.org-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maria_Grazia_Giammarinaro" title="Maria Grazia Giammarinaro">Maria Grazia Giammarinaro</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> a judge in the Criminal Court of Rome, took Office as the Special Representative in March 2010. From 2006 to 2009 this Office was held by <a href="/wiki/Eva_Biaudet" title="Eva Biaudet">Eva Biaudet</a>, a former Finnish Minister of Health and Social Services. Biaudet currently serves as Finnish Ombudsman for Minorities. Her predecessor was former Austrian Minister Helga Conrad, who served as the first OSCE Special Representative for Combating Trafficking in Human Beings.\n</p><p>The activities around Combating Trafficking in Human Beings in the OSCE Region of the Office of the Special Representative include:<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Co-operation with governments, helping them to accept and act on their responsibilities for curbing trafficking in human beings;</li>\n<li>Providing governments with decision and policy-making aids and offering guidance on anti-trafficking management, with the aim of arriving at solutions tailored to the needs of the individual countries and in line with international standards;</li>\n<li>Assisting governments to develop the national anti-trafficking structures required for efficient internal and transnational co-operation;</li>\n<li>Raising awareness to draw attention to the complexity of the problem and to the need for comprehensive solutions;</li>\n<li>Considering all dimensions of <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>, namely trafficking for <a href="/wiki/Sexual_exploitation" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual exploitation">sexual exploitation</a>, trafficking for <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced labour">forced and bonded labour</a>, including domestic servitude, trafficking into <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriages</a>, trafficking in organs and trafficking in children;</li>\n<li>Ensuring the effective interaction of all agents and stake holders involved in the fight against human trafficking, ranging from governmental authorities, law enforcement officials to NGOs, and\xe2\x80\x94last but not least\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/International_organization" title="International organization">international organizations</a>, as the agencies providing support thorough expertise and know-how;</li>\n<li>Guaranteeing the highest possible visibility of the OSCE\'s fight against human trafficking to focus attention on the issue.</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Democratization</dt></dl>\n<p>The OSCE claims to promote democracy and assist the participating states in building <a href="/wiki/Democratization" title="Democratization">democratic institutions</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Education</dt></dl>\n<p>Education programmes are an integral part of the organization\'s efforts in conflict prevention and post-conflict rehabilitation.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Elections</dt></dl>\n<p>As part of its democratization activities, the OSCE carries out election assistance projects in the run-up to, during, and following elections. However, the effectiveness of such assistance is arguable\xe2\x80\x94Kazakhstan, for example, despite being the former chair of the OSCE, is considered by many to be one of the least democratic countries in the world. Moreover, the recent democratic advances made in other Central Asian republics, notably Kyrgyzstan, have led to rumours of Soviet-style disruption of the Kyrgyz democratic process by, in particular, Kazakhstan and Russia. This may be in large part due to fears over the long-term stability of these countries\' own quasi-dictatorships.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Gender equality</dt></dl>\n<p>The equality of men and women is an integral part of sustainable democracy. The OSCE aims to provide equal opportunities for men and women and to integrate <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a> in policies and practices.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Human rights</dt></dl>\n<p>The OSCE\'s <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> activities focus on such priorities as <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement" title="Freedom of movement">freedom of movement</a> and religion, preventing torture and trafficking in persons.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>National and international NGOs</dt></dl>\n<p>OSCE could grant <a href="/wiki/Consultative_Status" class="mw-redirect" title="Consultative Status">consultive status</a> to <a href="/wiki/NGOs" class="mw-redirect" title="NGOs">NGOs</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_nongovernmental_organizations" class="mw-redirect" title="International nongovernmental organizations">INGOs</a> in the form of "Researcher-in-residence programme" (run by the Prague Office of the OSCE Secretariat): accredited representatives of national and international NGOs are granted access to all records and to numerous topical compilations related to OSCE field activities.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Media freedom</dt></dl>\n<p>The OSCE observes relevant media developments in its participating states with a view to addressing and providing early warning on violations of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of expression">freedom of expression</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Minority rights</dt></dl>\n<p>Ethnic conflict is one of the main sources of large-scale violence in Europe today. The OSCE\'s approach is to identify and to seek early resolution of ethnic tensions, and to set standards for the rights of persons belonging to <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minority groups</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_on_National_Minorities" title="High Commissioner on National Minorities">High Commissioner on National Minorities</a> has been established.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="OSCE_Democracy_Defender_Award">OSCE Democracy Defender Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: OSCE Democracy Defender Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Democracy Defender Award honors a person or group for contributions to the promotion of democracy and the defense of human rights "in the spirit of Helsinki Final Act and other OSCE principles and commitments." The award was established in 2016 on the initiative of Ambassadors of 8 countries, and supported by the delegations of the 18 countries of the OSCE (22 countries in 2017).<sup id="cite_ref-demdefend_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demdefend-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-epde_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epde-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="text-align:center">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col" width="50" style="background:#87CEFA;">Year\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="150" style="background:#87CEFA;">Recipient\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="150" style="background:#87CEFA;">Nationality\n</th>\n<th scope="col" class="unsortable" width="250" style="background:#87CEFA;">Notes\n</th>\n<th scope="col" class="unsortable" width="80" style="background:#87CEFA;">Reference\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2017\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Golos_(election_monitor)" title="Golos (election monitor)">Golos</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>\n</td>\n<td>Russian organisation established in 2000 to protect the electoral rights of citizens and to foster civil society\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-demdefend_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demdefend-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2016\n</td>\n<td>Oleksandra Matviychuk\n</td>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>\n</td>\n<td>Ukrainian activist, coordinator of Euromaidan SOS and leader of Civil Rights Center\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-pravda.ua_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pravda.ua-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Following an unprecedented period of activity in the 1990s and early 2000s (decade), the OSCE has in the past few years faced accusations from the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> states (primarily<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Why primarily? (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>) of being a tool for the Western states to advance their own interests. For instance, the events in <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> in 2004 (the "<a href="/wiki/Orange_Revolution" title="Orange Revolution">Orange Revolution</a>") led to allegations by Russia of OSCE involvement on behalf of the pro-Western <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yushchenko" title="Viktor Yushchenko">Viktor Yushchenko</a>. At the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Munich_Conference_on_Security_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Munich Conference on Security Policy">Munich Conference on Security Policy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> made this position very clear:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd>"They [unnamed Western States] are trying to transform the OSCE into a vulgar instrument designed to promote the foreign policy interests of one or a group of countries. And this task is also being accomplished by the OSCE\'s bureaucratic apparatus, which is absolutely not connected with the state founders in any way. Decision-making procedures and the involvement of so-called non-governmental organizations are tailored for this task. These organizations are formally independent but they are purposefully financed and therefore under control".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>Russia and its allies are advancing the concept of a comprehensive OSCE reform, which would make the Secretariat, institutions and field presences more centralized and accountable to collective consensus-based bodies and focus the work of the Organization on topical security issues (human trafficking, terrorism, non-proliferation, arms control, etc.), at the expense of the "Human Dimension", or human rights issues. The move to reduce the autonomy of the theoretically independent OSCE institutions, such as ODIHR, would effectively grant a Russian veto over any OSCE activity. Western participating States are opposing this process, which they see as an attempt to prevent the OSCE from carrying out its democratization agenda in post-Soviet countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2008_U.S._presidential_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 U.S. presidential election">2008 U.S. presidential election</a>, OSCE\'s ODIHR was accused of having double standards by Russia\'s lawmaker Slutsky. The point was made that while numerous violations of the voting process were registered, its criticism came only from within the United States (media, human rights organizations, McCain\'s election staff), while the OSCE known for its bashing criticism of elections on the post-Soviet space remained silent.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="OSCE_Parliamentary_Assembly">OSCE Parliamentary Assembly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: OSCE Parliamentary Assembly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2004 the OSCE Parliamentary Assembly sent <a href="/wiki/Election_observer" class="mw-redirect" title="Election observer">election observers</a> to the U.S. Presidential elections. The OSCE Parliamentary Assembly\xe2\x80\x99s president at the time was Democratic Congressman <a href="/wiki/Alcee_Hastings" title="Alcee Hastings">Alcee Hastings</a>. Hastings had previously been impeached for corruption by the U.S. Congress. The OSCE faced criticism of partisanship and double standards due to Hastings\'s past and the fact that the OSCE\'s mandate was to promote democracy and the values of civil society.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010 the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> was criticized from within by the Latvian delegation for lacking transparency and democracy. <a href="/wiki/R._Spencer_Oliver" title="R. Spencer Oliver">Spencer Oliver</a> (b. 1938) secretary general of the OSCE Parliamentary Assembly, who has held the post since the organization\'s inception in 1992, faced a challenge from the Latvian <a href="/wiki/Artis_Pabriks" title="Artis Pabriks">Artis Pabriks</a>. According to the rules of the OSCE Parliamentary Assembly the incumbent general secretary can only be replaced with a full consensus minus one. Pabriks called the rules "quite shocking from the perspective of an organization that\'s monitoring elections".<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Ilkka_Kanerva" title="Ilkka Kanerva">Ilkka Kanerva</a> was elected the president of the OSCE PA. Kanerva had previously been fired from his post as foreign minister of Finland after lying about sending over 200 text messages to an erotic dancer.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_Texas_controversy">2012 Texas controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2012 Texas controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before the U.S. presidential elections of November 2012, the OSCE announced its intention to send electoral observers to Texas and to other <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. states</a>. This prompted the Attorney General of Texas <a href="/wiki/Greg_Abbott" title="Greg Abbott">Greg Abbott</a> to send letters to U.S. <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> and to the OSCE,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> threatening to arrest OSCE officials if they should enter electoral premises in Texas and break <a href="/wiki/Texas_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Texas law">Texas law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In reply, the U.S. Department of State stated that OSCE observers enjoyed immunities.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In the event, no incidents between OSCE and Texas authorities were recorded during the elections.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_in_Donbass">War in Donbass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: War in Donbass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_(16524364807).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_%2816524364807%29.jpg/220px-OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_%2816524364807%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_%2816524364807%29.jpg/330px-OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_%2816524364807%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_%2816524364807%29.jpg/440px-OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_%2816524364807%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2002" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OSCE_SMM_monitoring_the_movement_of_heavy_weaponry_in_eastern_Ukraine_(16524364807).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>OSCE SMM monitoring the movement of heavy weaponry in eastern Ukraine</div></div></div>\n<p>The organization has been criticized by the Ukrainian press and government for actions during the Russian\xe2\x80\x93Ukraine conflict. During the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">War in Donbass</a>, an OSCE observer allowed Russian separatists to use the organization\'s marked vehicle, which prompted the belief that the OSCE was biased in the war and not interested in carrying out its duties of mediating a ceasefire. The organization issued a statement regretting the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The organization has also been criticized by Ukraine for allegedly failing to monitor the implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Minsk_Protocol" title="Minsk Protocol">Minsk Protocol</a>. The agreement called for a creation of a 40&#160;km buffer zone, but upon Ukrainian forces withdrawing from their 20&#160;km portion of the buffer, Russian separatists are said to have simply occupied the abandoned territory without withdrawing from their own 20&#160;km buffer.  Likewise, there are allegations of separatists using OSCE marked vehicles for transportation. Moreover, the mission also received criticism alleging that only 2 checkpoints on the Russian\xe2\x80\x93Ukrainian border are currently being monitored, which has been described as "seriously inadequate" by Daniel Baerm the US ambassador to the OSCE.\n</p><p>On the other hand, Ukraine has faced criticism following a BBC report showing an alleged violation of the Minsk agreement when Ukraine stationed tanks in the residential neighborhood Avdeevka. <sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The mission has also been criticized for waiting  months to deploy drones to help monitor the border as well as withdrawing them after only several weeks of use due to Russian electronic attacks. Ukraine has argued that approximately 80% of the OSCE observers located near <a href="/wiki/Mariupol" title="Mariupol">Mariupol</a> were Russian citizens and many had ties to Russian security agencies such as the FSB and GRU. The organization has also been accused of allegedly revealing the locations of Ukrainian troops to Russian forces during the conflict and that Russian OSCE observers may be directly coordinating separatist artillery strikes on Ukrainian positions.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 December 2014, an OSCE observer was injured by Ukrainian counter artillery fire while observing militants firing at Ukrainian forces. The OSCE team was located next to two pro-Russian mortar teams. The OSCE team did not radio in or record the Russian mortar team firing on Ukrainian positions. Critics stated that the unorthodox behavior of being located next to an active separatist artillery position and not reporting the incident showed that the OSCE team was not acting in an impartial manner.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 October 2015 a suspended OSCE monitor confirmed he was a former employee of Russia\'s <a href="/wiki/Main_Intelligence_Directorate" title="Main Intelligence Directorate">Main Intelligence Directorate</a>. The suspended SMM stated he had no trouble receiving the position and neither the OSCE nor Ukraine\'s Security Service thoroughly checked his background.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Following the report the OSCE issued a comment stating the monitor has been fired due to violations of the organization\'s code of conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> On 6 April 2016 photos of OSCE  monitors attending the wedding of a Russian separatist were found. The wedding was hosted in June 2015.  The OSCE expressed regret over the incident, issuing a statement saying "The unprofessional behavior displayed by the monitors in the picture is an individual incident that should not be abused to cast a shadow on the reputation of other mission members." The OSCE reported that the monitors were no longer with the OSCE special monitoring mission.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2017 an OSCE vehicle struck a mine, killing one member and injuring two.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Two armoured vehicles were on patrol was near <a href="/wiki/Luhansk" title="Luhansk">Luhansk</a> when one struck the mine.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT01_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT01-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The dead man was American while the injured woman was from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and the other person was from the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT01_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT01-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 July 2018 it was revealed that Russian intelligence services received inside information about the activities of the OSCE Special Monitoring Mission to Ukraine from a staff member of the OSCE. The insider information consisted of observer\'s preference to alcohol, women, their financial situation, and their contacts in Ukraine. The OSCE issued a statement expressing concern over the alleged security breach.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In April 2017, Turkish President <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan">Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan</a> criticized the OSCE for reporting that opposition "No" campaigners in the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_constitutional_referendum,_2017" title="Turkish constitutional referendum, 2017">Turkish constitutional referendum</a> had faced bans, police interventions and arrests. Erdo\xc4\x9fan said: "Now the Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe says if the result is \xe2\x80\x98yes\xe2\x80\x99, that means there are a lot of problems. Who are you? First of all, you should know your place. This is not your duty."<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In February 2018, OSCE has criticized the Turkish government over the detention of social media users for criticizing the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_military_operation_in_Afrin" title="Turkish military operation in Afrin">Turkish invasion of northern Syria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; Europe</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Western_European_Union" title="Western European Union">Western European Union</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
